Summary 130:
Ensuring that appliances and fittings comply with the requirements of Directive 2009/142/EC on the harmonisation of the technical characteristics of gaseous fuels (see summary) (European Union rules on the sale and putting into service of appliances and fitting) (See amending act(s) below)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1025/2012 on the conformity assessment of electrical and electronic appliances
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to harmonise the technical requirements of the EU’s legislation on the placing into service, installation and use of gas-powered appliances.
It sets out the technical specifications of those requirements, especially with regard to the design, manufacture, operation, testing, the rational use of energy and installation of appliances. It does not cover risks caused by appliances in the case of incorrect installation, maintenance or use.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
electrical appliances, whether new or second-hand, imported from a non-EU country;
any appliance and fitting imported into the EU from outside the EU.
Manufacturers must ensure that they only make available on the market appliances or fittings which are in conformity with this regulation.
Importers and importers must ensure they only place into service those appliances which meet the requirements laid down in the regulation. They must also ensure that:
the appliance or fitting bears the CE conformity marking;
the manufacturer provides sufficient and detailed information on the intended use of the appliance so as to allow it to be installed and put into service;
they ensure that its handling does not adversely affect its compliance.
the gas supply conditions do not constitute barriers to trade and that they do not restrict the putting in service of the appliances that are compatible with the local gas conditions.
EU declaration of conformity
An appliance or a fitting bearing the CE marking must be available in a single EU declaration on the EU market. This declaration must be published in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJ). It must be accompanied by a reference number (reference number) for each type of gas family and gas group used on the territory of each EU Member State.
The declaration must contain the following information:
name of the manufacturer and the name of the importer;
type and nature of the gas families and gas groups used on their territory;
description of the types of gas and supply pressures used in the Member States.
In addition, the declaration must include:
a description of the type and quantity of gas used in each Member State;
a list of the different types of gases used in different Member States;
details of the requirements for the design and manufacture of appliances;
requirements for the operation and testing of appliances, including for the use of electricity;
measures to reduce energy consumption in different areas, including in buildings.
Exemptions
Member States may exclude from the scope of the regulation certain appliances which do not comply with certain essential requirements. However, they may exempt certain appliances from the regulation, such as those which:
have been manufactured in a Member State other than that of the Member State in which they are located;
have not been certified by the competent authority;
do not meet the essential requirements of this regulation;
are not covered by the Annex II of the directive on harmonised standards.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 July 2012.
BACKGROUND
Directive 2009/146/EC of the Council of the 21 May 2009 on the Harmonisation of Certain Gas-Fuelled Combustion Products (known as the ‘new approach’ principles) (recast) is based on the principles set out in the Council Resolution of 7 May 1985 on a new approach to technical harmonisation and standards. It sets out common principles and reference provisions intended to apply across sectoral legislation in order to provide a coherent basis for revision or recasts of that legislation.
For more information, see:
Electrical and Electronic Appliances (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Gas-fuelled appliance: a device that emits or emits gases.
* Electrical and electronic appliance: any appliance or device that is intended to be placed into service.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Decision 2010/1025/EU of 21 May 2010 on the approximation of certain technical requirements relating to the sale of certain electrical appliances and of certain electronic fittings in accordance with the provisions of Council Regulation (EC) No 1024/2008/EC (see consolidated version).
* Conformity assessment: the assessment of the conformity of an appliance or of an electronic device to the relevant EU acts.

Summary 131:
Cross-border transport of euro cash by road: rules for the transport of the cash in-transit (CIT) companies
Cross-Border transport of Euro Cash by Road
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1072/2009 — rules for cross-border travel of the euro cash in transport by road between participating EU countries
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules on the transport and authorisation of the professional transport of cash in the euro area by road.
It aims to ensure that professional cash handlers, banks, the large retail sector and other professionals working in the sector can contract with a CIT company that offers the best price and/or service and to take advantage of the services of the nearest national central bank (NCB) branch or CIT cash centre, even if it is located in another EU country.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
cross-border CIT companies operating in the European Economic Area (EEA) participating in the Schengen area (now the EU).
Companies wishing to transport euro cash must apply for a licence from the granting authority in its EU country of origin.
The CIT licence must be valid for a period of 5 years and must include the following information:
the number of operations that may be carried out in the host EU country following the international carriage from another country;
the type of CIT vehicle and the number of cabotage operations within 7 days.
the minimum rates of pay for each CIT worker.
a minimum number of euro deliveries/pick-ups per day.
EU countries must ensure that CIT vehicles are registered in their territory and that the issuing authority issues the licence.
A company wishing to operate in the EEA must:
apply for a cross-Border crossing licence from its EU Member State of origin;
be registered in the country in which it is established;
have a valid CIT driving licence issued by the authority in the Member State in charge of issuing the licence;
ensure that the company is registered in a Member State with the same number of employees as the company in question.
In addition, the company must provide the competent authorities with:
a copy of the CIT driver’s licence and a certificate;
a certificate of authorisation from the competent authority of the host Member State;
certificates of safety and security of the vehicle and of the staff;
proof that the driving licence is valid for at least 3 years.
CIT vehicles must be equipped with at least one of the following:
two standard weapons*;
one or more standard weapons;
two or more light-duty vehicles equipped with a standard weapon;
at least one or more armed staff with a valid cross-board weapon.
Licence holders must be:
certified by a national authority;
registered in the EU country in whose territory they are established.
They must be able to carry out the following tasks:
transport euro cash from one Member State to another;
carry out euro cash deliveries and pick-ups in a host country during the same day;
take part in the exchange of information between the authorities of the two Member States;
assist in the inspection of the vehicles;
participate in the training of staff in accordance with the rules laid down in the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 21 October 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* CIT: a company that transports euro cash on the road between Member States.
* Cross-border: a transport company that carries out the transport, delivery or pick-up of euros in cash in a vehicle.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 			
Commission Implementing Decision (EU) 2020/852 of 21 October 2020 on the application of Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 1024/2009 of the European Parliament and the Council on the common rules for access to the international road haulage market for the crossing of the road of the Euro Area (OJ L 183, 21.10.2020, pp. 1-2)

Summary 133:
Euro coins — circulation and commemorative coins
Euro coins – circulation and collector coins
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 975/98 on the issuance of euro coins
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules on the circulation and 2-euro commemorative euro coins.
It aims to ensure that euro coins are issued in a uniform way throughout the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU countries whose currency is the euro.
EU countries may issue two types of euro coin: circulation coins, which are intended to commemorate a specific subject, and collector coins which are not issued with a view to their entry into circulation.
Issuance of circulation coins:
circulation coins are coins denominated in euro and cent and complying with the denominations and technical specifications laid down by the Council.
Collector coins are euro coins intended for collection.
The issuances of collector coins must be accounted for on an aggregated basis in the volume of coin issuance to be approved by the European Central Bank.
In addition, EU countries may also issue 2 euro commemorative coin to celebrate specific subjects, subject to limits set per year and per issuing EU country for the number of issues of such coins. The total number of coins put into circulation for each individual issue must not exceed the higher of the following two ceilings:
0,1 % of the cumulated total net number of 2 euro coins put in circulation up to the beginning of the year preceding the end of the calendar year preceding issue.
1.5 % of 1- and 2.
2.5% of the total net numbers of 2-centre numismatic euro coins in circulation
3.5%.
The Commission must conduct a cost-benefit analysis on the continued issuance of the 2- and 1-euro coins, taking into account the real production costs of those coins set against their value and benefits. The Commission should also conduct an impact assessment on the continuing issuance of 1 euro coins and 2 euro coin collector coins. This analysis should be carried out in accordance with Regulation (EU) 2019/852 on the issue of euro notes.

Summary 134:
The European Social Fund (ESF) — mission and scope
The European social fund (ESA)
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — mission, scope and objectives of the European Social Facility
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out the ESF’s mission and its objectives.
The ESF supports the European Union (EU), the Member States and the regions in pursuing the priorities and headline targets of the EU strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth (the ‘Europe 2020 strategy’), as well as their specific challenges with regard to achieving the Europe 2020 strategy objectives. It also contributes to the sustainable recovery of the economy.
KEY POINTS
The regulation defines the mission and the scope of the ESA, together with the related investment priorities addressing the thematic objectives, and lays down specific provisions concerning the type of activities that may be financed by the ESA. The ESF is responsible for:
promoting the better functioning of labour markets by enhancing the transnational geographical mobility of workers;
improving the quality of education and training;
encouraging gender equality, the economic independence of women, education and skills upgrading and the reintegration of female victims of violence into the labour market and into society;
contributing to the fight against social exclusion and combating poverty;
supporting cross-sectoral and territorial-based partnerships.
In line with Article 9 TFEU, ESF objectives, the ESA activities are based on:
the promotion of a high levels of employment, the guarantee of adequate social protection and a high level of education, training and protection of human health;
the fight against poverty, including the inclusion of disadvantaged people such as the Roma;
raising awareness of the importance of social inclusion and combating social exclusion.
EU Member States are encouraged to leverage ESF financial instruments in order to support, for example, students, job creation, job mobility, social inclusion, social entrepreneurship and social entrepreneurship.
Activities
The ESA supports the design and implementation of policies and actions in connection with its missions, taking account of the relevant Integrated Guidelines and relevant country-specific recommendations adopted in accordance with Article 121(2) and 148(4) of the Treaty on European Union.
EURES activities
EurES activities are organised by the European network of employment services, in relation to recruitment and related information, advice and guidance services at national and cross-border level. They aim to improve the quality and effectiveness of the recruitment process and to improve employability in the European labour market. They also aim to:
increase the participation of women in the labour markets;
facilitate the integration of young people into the workforce;
promote the integration and mobility of people with disabilities;
strengthen the social inclusion of people from disadvantaged groups;
ensure that specific actions are taken to promote gender equality.
Cooperation between Member States, the regions and ESF projects
The EU countries and the ESA is encouraged to develop partnerships with the social partners, such as local, regional and local authorities, to achieve the objectives set out in this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
 			
The purpose of this regulation is to set out the objectives and the specific ESF activities.
For more information, see:
European Social Fund — Mission and scope (European Commission).

Summary 137:
Reform of the Common Fisheries Fund (CFP) (2013-2020)
Reformation of the common fisheries fund (2013 - 2020)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 on the European Maritime Fund (EMFF)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It repeals and repeals Council Regulation (EC) No 2328/2003 and its subsequent amendments.
It aims to modernise and streamline the common fishery fund, the Common Maritime Fund, which is responsible for managing the EU’s fisheries policy.
KEY POINTS
The EMFF is one of the main instruments of the EU fisheries policy and is managed by the European Commission. It covers the Baltic Sea, North Sea, Celtic Seas, Bay of Biscay and the Iberian Coast, Mediterranean and Black Sea sea basins.
The regulation repeals the previous CFP and its previous amendments, which had been amended several times. It repeals, in particular:
Council Regulation No 1380/2013 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 17 June 2013 on the common Fisheries Fund;
Decision No 1255/2011 establishing the European Agricultural Fund for Rural Development (EAFRD) and the European Economic and Social Funds (ESI Funds);
Decisions No 1261/2006 and No 1198/2006 establishing the Common Fund for Maritime and Fisheries (CPF) and repealing Council Regulations No 791/2007 and No 1254/2007 (see summary).
The new EMFF was established in 2013. The EMFF supports the implementation of the Integrated Maritime Policy (IMP), which aims to:
ensure the sustainable management of Europe's oceans and seas;
improve the efficiency of fishing activities;
reduce the impact of climate change on the marine environment;
promote the sustainable development of the maritime and fisheries sectors;
increase employment and territorial cohesion;
foster marketing and processing;
encourage the development of marine research and innovation;
contribute to the sustainable use of marine resources;
support the development and management of systems for the monitoring and evaluation of marine biological resources.
EMFF operational programme
EU countries must draw up an operational programme for the EMFF, which must be consistent with the priorities of the Union adopted by the Commission for that policy area. It must cover:
fishing activities in the Baltic and North Sea;
the management of different sectoral policies in the Celtic Seas;
management of the management of fisheries in the Black Sea; and
fisheries in the Mediterranean, Black Sea and Iberia.
EU financial support
EU Member States must ensure that:
the EMFF does not provide financial support to operators of vessels engaged in illegal, unreported and unregulated (IUU) fishing or of vessels flagged to countries identified as non-cooperating third countries as set out in this regulation.
Member States must also ensure that the financial support is not disbursed to operators who, ex ante, did not comply with requirements related to the public interest and conservation of marine marine resources. In addition, Member States are required to take the necessary measures to prevent ineligible payments from being made.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
For more information, see:
European Maritime Fund
European Fishing Fund (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Common Fisheries Facility: a multiannual financial framework for the European Union (EU).

Summary 138:
Transparency of investment products offered to retail investors (PRIIPs)
Transparency and investor protection — PRIIPs
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/852 laying down uniform rules on the transparency and disclosure of investment opportunities for retail investors
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that investment opportunities* offered by the financial services industry are transparent, fair, clear and not misleading to consumers.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
investment opportunities* that are manufactured by financial services companies for the purpose of providing investment opportunities, where the amount repayable to the retail investor is subject to fluctuation because of exposure to reference values, or subject to the performance of one or more assets which are not directly purchased by the investor.
It does not apply to investment opportunities that do not offer investment opportunities and deposits solely exposed to interest rates.
To meet the needs of retail investors, the regulation lays down rules on:
the key information document (KID) which must be produced by entities operating in the banking, insurance, securities and fund sectors of the financial markets;
the format, presentation and content of the KID;
information on social or environmental outcomes sought by the PRIIP manufacturer.
The KID must be drawn up in a standardised format which allows retail investors to compare different products. It must also allow for use of electronic communications where appropriate having regard to the circumstances of the transaction.
EU countries must designate the competent authorities responsible for that supervision.
PRIIP manufacturers and persons advising on, or selling them must comply with all the relevant requirements of the regulation. They must also inform the competent authority of the EU country in which they are located.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2018. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2019.

Summary 139:
Resolution of failing banks in the European Union: Single Resolution Mechanism (SRM)
Resolving failed banks within the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1024/2013 on the resolution of banks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a centralised resolution mechanism for all banks operating in the Member States participating in the Single Supervisory Mechanism.
It aims to ensure that the resolution decisions made by Member States’ national authorities are consistent and transparent.
KEY POINTS
The resolution mechanism (SSM) is based on the European System of Supervision and Resolution Mechanisms (ESRSM).
The SSM is the only resolution mechanism in the EU that is open to all Member States. It is designed to ensure a neutral approach in dealing with failing banks and therefore increase stability of the banks of the participating Member States and prevent the spill-over of crises into non-participating Member States, thus facilitating the functioning of the internal market as a whole.
The European Central Bank (ECB) is the sole supervisor of the SSM. Although the ECB will not supervise those institutions on a solo basis, it will be the only supervisor that will have a global perception of the risk which a group, and indirectly its individual members, is exposed to. The ECB is responsible for the supervision of the EU’s banking sector.
Member States are required to transfer to the Fund the contributions that they raise at national level in accordance with Directive 2014/59/EU and this regulation. The European Stability and Financial Stability Facility (ESFSP) is also an integral part of the scheme.
In addition, the European Commission is an observer in the resolution decision-making process. The Commission and the Council of the Union are also involved in the implementation of the resolution resolution mechanism.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EU has been working towards a single resolution mechanism since 2013.
For more information, see:
Resolution mechanism (European Commission).

Directive 2014/58/EU

Summary 140:
Noise-related operating restrictions at European Union airports
Noise - related operating restrictions
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2013 on noise-related air traffic management
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to reduce the noise impact from aircraft at EU airports.
It sets out the procedure for the imposition of operating restrictions.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all airports in the European Union (EU). It does not apply to airports located in non-EU countries.
A Member State in which an airport is located must designate one or more competent authorities responsible for the process to be followed when adopting an operating restriction. These authorities must be independent of any organisation which could be affected by the action.
The competent authorities must also ensure that local residents, or their representatives, and relevant local authorities are consulted, and that technical information on noise measures is provided to them.
Where a noise problem has been identified, additional noise abatement measures should be identified in accordance with the balanced approach methodology. These measures should not lead to delay in the implementation of operational measures which could immediately alleviate the noise problem without substantially affecting the operational capacity of an airport.
In addition, Member States, or airport managing bodies, as appropriate, may offer economic incentives to encourage aircraft operators to use less noisy aircraft during the transitional period referred to in point (4) of Article 2 of the regulation.
Member States must ensure that:
airport operators are consulted in a transparent way on the intended actions;
the measures are adopted and sufficient notification is provided;
measures are implemented;
dispute resolution is provided for.
Airport managing bodies must communicate with the European Commission and the European Aviation Safety Agency (EASA).
The European Commission is responsible for implementing the regulation in the field of noise management. The Commission may adopt delegated acts for technical updates through delegated acts as appropriate.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMISSION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
   
 
The noise situation at airports is one of the main challenges facing the EU. It is a major factor in the development of the EU’s air transport system. The regulation aims to improve the soundness of the air transport network and to reduce noise.
For more information, see:
Air traffic management (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Air traffic management: the management of air traffic at an airport in order to ensure the effective functioning of EU transport systems and the protection of the environment.
* Noise: the noise emitted by aircraft and ground equipment in the vicinity of the airport. It includes the noise generated by the aircraft and the noise produced by the ground equipment.

  Еганскабранка гараца нарка  хракова

Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) no 681 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 141:
Cross-border insolvency proceedings: rules for the administration of cross-border proceedings
Cross-Border insolvencies: rights of creditors
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/852 — rules for cross-Border proceedings
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It aims to improve the application of certain of its provisions in order to enhance the effective administration and coordination of proceedings in the event of insolvent insolvent debtor’s assets.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all insolvent persons, legal persons and companies, irrespective of whether they are a natural person or a legal person, a trader or an individual.
It does not apply to:
legal persons;
legal entities;
individuals;
businesses;
other legal entities.
Objectives
The purpose of the regulation is to ensure that proceedings are carried out in accordance with the law of the European Union (EU).
It also aims to prevent the transfer of assets or judicial proceedings from one EU country to another, to obtain a more favourable legal position to the detriment of the general body of creditors (forum shopping).
In addition, the regulation sets out the conditions for:
the opening of proceedings;
the involvement of a judicial body (i.e. a court or body empowered by national law to open proceedings);
the right of the creditor to intervene in proceedings; and
the rights of the creditors to be heard in proceedings.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCELEGAL FORCE
This regulation entered into force on 1 July 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission published a report on the implementation of this regulation in June 2018.
For more information, see:
‘The European Union’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 142:
Liability of carriers and their passengers in the event of a maritime accident
Liability and compensation for passengers involved in maritime accidents
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2012 on the liability of carriers by sea and passengers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a single set of rules governing the rights of carriers* and passengers* in the case of an accident.
It applies to the carriage of passengers by sea within a single EU country on board ships of Classes A and B under Article 4 of Directive 98/18/EC, and lays down certain supplementary requirements.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
passengers carried in a ship:
under a contract of carriage;
who, with the consent of the carrier, is accompanying a vehicle or live animals which are covered by a contract;
the IMO Reservation and Guidelines for Implementation of the Athens Convention adopted by the Legal Committee of the International Maritime Organisation on 19 October 2006.
The liability of a carrier and a performing carrier is governed by Article 3(3) of the Convention relating to the Carriage of Passengers and their Luggage by Sea, 1974 and the Protocol of 2002 to the Convention.
Passengers are entitled to compensation in respect of:
the loss of mobility equipment or other specific equipment used by a passenger with reduced mobility,
the damage caused to passengers’ mobility equipment,
damage caused to their luggage.
In addition, the carrier and performing carrier must provide passengers with at least the information contained in a summary of the provisions of the regulation prepared by the European Commission and made public. This information must be made available to the public and to the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union (EU).
The European Commission may adopt measures, in accordance with the principle of subsidiarity as set out in Article 5 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU, to settle disputes between the EU and the European Economic Area countries. These measures should include liability rules for damage caused by passengers, since it is important to ensure that a proper level of compensation is paid.
EU countries may choose to defer application of this regulation until 4 years after the date of its application.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 31 December 2012. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 31 December 2013.
BACKGROUND
 
The Convention on the Rights of Carriers by Sea (Athens Convention) applies to international transport only.
For more information, see:
The Athens Convention (European Commission).

Summary 143:
Establishment of rail freight corridors (Regulation (EC) No 2137/85) and the management of freight corridors in the European Union
Establishment and management of railway freight corridors
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/2137 — establishing and managing rail freight networks
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a framework for the establishment, management and operation of freight freight networks in the EU.
It aims to improve the efficiency of the rail freight transport relative to other modes of transport.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the conditions for the selection of further freight corridors.
The European Commission must consult the European Economic Interest Grouping (EEIG), a European economic interest grouping, and the Committee of European Union Member States on the establishment of the freight corridor.
Each Member State must establish a freight corridor at the latest 2 years after the decision of the Commission.
Member States must establish an executive board responsible for defining the general objectives of the corridor, supervising and taking the measures as expressly provided for in Article 7 of the regulation, and in Article 9 and 11 of the annex to the regulation.
An executive board is responsible for:
monitoring and evaluating the performance of the railway freight services along the corridor;
ensuring the availability of capacity, fluid movements and a coherent application of priority rules to the different types of traffic in the event of disturbance;
coordinating the activities of the infrastructure managers;
organising the development of intermodal freight terminals;
the coordination of freight services between the terminals.
In addition to the executive board, an advisory board is set up. It may take the form of an economic interest group, which may also coordinate its activities in order to ensure, on the corridors concerned, the availability and fluid movements of freight trains.
A committee composed of representatives of the Member States, the EEIG and the European Commission, advises the Commission on the implementation of this regulation. The committee may issue an advisory recommendation to the Commission, which then adopts a decision to establish a new freight corridor or to prolong an existing one.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLACE?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
The EU has been developing a rail freight market for more than 20 years. Although the opening of the market has made it possible for new operators to enter the rail market, market mechanisms have not been and are not sufficient to organise, regulate and secure rail freight traffic.
For more information, see:
Rail freight networks (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Delegated Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/1125 of 21 December 2018 establishing and governing rail freight network (OJ L 347, 28.12.2018, pp. 1-8)

Road transport operators — common rules for the occupation of road transport operator
Road transport authorities — common requirements for the exercise of the occupation OF ROAD TRANSPORT OPERATOR
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 596/2002 — common conditions for the application of the occupational qualification of the road transport operators
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the common rules governing the qualification and professional competence of the European Union (EU) road transport transport operators.
It aims to improve the quality of transport services in the EU and to improve road safety.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
any natural person, any legal person, whether profit-making or not, any association or group of persons without legal personality, or any official body, whether having its own legal personality or being dependent upon an authority having such personality, engaged in the transport of passengers, freight with a commercial purpose;
any other natural or legal person engaged in a transport of freight with an economic purpose.
In addition, it applies to undertakings engaged in:
the occupation of a road haulage operator solely by means of motor vehicles or combinations of vehicles the permissible laden mass of which does not exceed 3.5 tonnes;
the operation of a transport company, which is established in one or more than one EU country;
other undertakings established in several EU countries, which are fully carried out in those regions by undertakings operating there.
EU countries may decide to lower the number of undertakings and/or the size of the total fleet of vehicles which a person may manage.
Procedures of the person concerned must satisfy the conditions laid down in the regulation in order to pursue the occupation. The regulation does not apply to the following undertakings:
undertakings operating in the territory of a non-EU country, in which there is a single model certificate issued by the EU country of establishment;
individuals who have continuous experience in managing transport activities;
organised transport undertakings which are established in the territories of an EU country.

Summary 145:
Social security: coordination rules between EU countries’ social security systems
Social security rules: coordination systems
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 883/2004 on the application of social security schemes to employed persons and their families moving within the EU
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the coordination of the social security system between the European Union (EU) Member States’ institutions and the European Commission.
It aims to reduce the time needed for social security claims to be paid.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all EU citizens who are entitled to social security benefits, irrespective of their place of residence.
EU countries must:
cooperate in determining the place of residency of persons to whom this regulation and Regulation (EC’s No 882/2004 apply and, in the event of a dispute, take into consideration all relevant criteria to resolve the matter.
The Member States must provide or exchange all data necessary for establishing and determining the rights and obligations of persons who are covered by the regulation.
In their communications with the persons concerned, the relevant institutions must use the arrangements appropriate to each case, and favour the use of electronic means as far as possible.
Where there is doubt about the validity of a document or the accuracy of the facts on which the particulars contained therein are based, the institution of the Member State that receives the document must ask the issuing institution for the necessary clarification and, where appropriate, the withdrawal of that document.
Member States must ensure that:
the relevant information is transmitted by electronic means;
the Member State of residence is notified to the Member States;
there is no dispute between the institutions or authorities of two or more Member States about which institution should provide the benefits in cash or in kind;
a person concerned who could claim benefits if there was no dispute is entitled, on a provisional basis, to the benefits provided for by the legislation applied by the institution in question.
If there is a difference of views between the authorities of 2 or more EU countries about whether the benefits should be provided in cash, in kind or in any other form, the person concerned should be entitled to benefits only from their Member States of residence, if that person does not reside on the territory of one of those Member States concerned.
When a Member State receives a request for assistance from another Member State regarding the recovery of benefits provided but not due, the recovery payments and contributions and the offsetting and assistance with recovery, the jurisdiction of the requested Member State is limited to actions regarding enforcement measures.
A Member State which receives the request must inform the other Member States and the Commission of the reasons for the request. The Member States are responsible for the implementation of the Regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2005.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve the coordination between Member States in the field of social protection. These include:
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 574/72 of 21 March 1972 fixing the procedure for implementing Council Regulation (EEC, No 1408/71 on social security for employed persons moving within Europe;
Regulating (EC), Euratom and Euratom Implementing Decision (EC, Eurathea) No 1201/2003 establishing the procedure to be followed by the European Social Security Agency (ESSA);
Commission Decision (Euratom) 2015/852 laying down the procedures for implementing Implementing Regulation(EU) No 605/2014 on the coordination rules of the Social Security System (EURAThea).
For more information, see:
‘Social security coordination rules’ on Euratom's website.

Summary 146:
Statistics on public health and health and safety at work: European statistical system (EHS)
Statistical system on public and occupational safety and health at work
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008/EC establishing a European statistical framework for the systematic production of Community statistics on the general health and social aspects of work
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a common framework for collecting and compiling European Union (EU) statistics on health and work at work.
It sets out the statistical methodologies and data collections to be developed for the compilation of these statistics.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries and the European Commission (Eurostat).
EU countries must compile data concerning public health* and health* at work from sources such as household surveys or similar surveys or survey modules, or national administrative or reporting sources.
Eurostat collects these data on a voluntary basis.
The statistics are used for structural indicators, sustainable development indicators and European Community Health Indicators (ECHI), as well as for the other sets of indicators which it is necessary to develop for the purpose of monitoring Community actions in the fields of public health.
National authorities must ensure that the data collected are consistent with the developments and achievements resulting from Community action in the field of health. They must also take into consideration the need for coordination, whenever relevant and possible, with international organisations and relevant to the collection of national data.
In addition, Eurostat must take into account the needs of international organisations such as the United Nations and the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Cooperation with the UN, the World Health Organisation (WHO) and the International Labour Organisation (ILO)
The European statistical activities of Eurostat are carried out in cooperation with UN and its special organisations, such as:
the World Health Organization (WHO);
the ILO;
the United Nations Economic Commission for Europe (ECEco); and
the OECD.
Quality and comparability of the data
The Commission is empowered to adopt implementing measures covering characteristics of certain subjects and their breakdown, the reference periods, intervals and time limits for data provision and the provision of metadata. The Commission must also adopt measures to ensure the protection of personal data by the EU institutions and bodies and on the free movement of such data in the context of the European statistical programme.

Quality of employment statistics in Europe (2007 - 2013)

Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 608/2007 on the quality of employment data
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?

recreational activities;
social security;
employment;
health and well-being;
education;
human health and long-term care;
cultural activities.
In addition, EU countries must provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with reports on quality of the data transmitted.
Eurostat may establish and coordinate sample schemes in order to produce Community estimates where national sample schemes do not meet the EU requirements with regard to quarterly data collection. The Commission may also adopt measures to supplement the data collected.

Summary 148:
Requirements for the type-approval of hydrogen-powered vehicles
Requirements for hydrogen propulsion
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 — requirements for the design, manufacture and installation of hydrogen components and systems for motor vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules on the design and manufacture of hydrogen vehicles.
It aims to ensure that hydrogen vehicles comply with the requirements of this regulation and its implementing measures.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
motor vehicles of categories M and N, as listed in the regulation’s annexes;
vehicles designed to use compressed (gaseous) hydrogen;
transport systems, components and separate technical units intended for such vehicles;
hydrogen components, other than containers, for which the technical specifications are laid down by implementing measures adopted in accordance with Council Decision 1999/468/EC of 28 June 1999 laying down the procedures for the exercise of implementing powers conferred on the European Commission.
General requirements
For the design of motor vehicles, the regulation sets out the requirements for:
the use of pure hydrogen or a mixture of hydrogen and natural gas/biomethane;
new forms of hydrogen storage or usage;
the impact protection of vehicles with regard to the integrity of the hydrogen system and its components.
Manufacturers must ensure that:
their products comply with all the requirements laid down in this regulation;
they have been tested and certified according to the test procedures set out in Annexes I and II of the regulation; and
they are installed in the vehicle.
in accordance with this regulation.
The Commission may adopt implementing measures for requirements relating to any of the following the following:
specifications for the use or mixture of pure and/or mixed hydrogen or natural gas and biomethanes;
requirements relating to the use of new forms of storage or use;
rules for the introduction of hydrogen systems and components into the vehicle;
conditions for the testing of hydrogen containers and systems.
Implementing measures
If the Commission considers that the regulation does not meet its objectives, it may adopt measures to supplement it.

Summary 149:
Ensuring equal market access to the internal market in natural gas
Enesco Regulation (EC) No 1775/2005 on conditions for access to natural gas transmission networks
Ensco Regulation(EC) 2017/849/EC on the conditions for the access of transmission system operators
SUMMARY
WHAT DOES THIS REGULATION DO?
It lays down rules to ensure that the European Union (EU) has a single market for natural gas.
It aims to create a level playing field for all natural gas suppliers in the EU.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
transmission system operators and third party access services;
the European Network of Transmission System Operators for Gas (ENTSO for Gas);
transport contracts;
information on the physical status and efficiency of the system;
transparency of operational decisions made by supply undertakings.
The ENTSO is responsible for:
monitoring the transmission system operator’s performance;
providing information on the overall demand and supply situation and identifying the reasons for movements in the wholesale price;
establishing the European Gas Transmission System Operator for Gas;
coordinating the network management of the gas transmission system and gas distribution system.
In addition, the regulation sets out the responsibilities of the European Commission.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATIONS APPLY?
Directive 2009/73/EC has applied since 1 January 2009.
   
It had to become law in the Member States by 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to achieve the objectives of the regulation. These include:
the creation of a single EU internal market for gas;
improving the transparency of the internal gas market;
reducing the fragmentation of the market and improving the efficiency of gas transmission systems.
For more information, see:
Natural gas regulation (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Transmission system operator: any natural gas system operator responsible for the transmission of natural gas from one Member State to another.
* Third party access service: any service provided by a third party to another Member State.
Transport contract: the terms and conditions of the transport contracts of a particular system operator in a Member State must be the same as those of another system operator, unless minimum requirements are set which must be met by all transport contracts.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 150:
Judicial cooperation in civil matters between EU countries and non-EU countries
Jurisdiction, recognition and enforcement of judgments in civil and commercial matters
Judiciary cooperation in Civil matters
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on the conclusion of agreements between the European Community and a third country on matters falling within the exclusive competence of the Community
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the European Union (EU) has exclusive competence to conclude agreements on matters relating to jurisdiction and the recognition and enforceability of judgments.
It sets out the conditions under which EU countries can conclude agreements with non-European Union countries.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all civil matters covered by Article 300 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU. It does not apply to certain regional agreements between a few EU countries, for example two or three, intended to address local situations and not open for accession to other countries, which are not covered by this regulation.
EU countries must notify the European Commission of ongoing or already announced negotiations with a view to obtaining an authorisation to open formal negotiations. The Commission must be kept fully informed throughout the different stages of the negotiations and should be allowed to participate as an observer in the negotiations as regards those matters.
The Commission may propose negotiating guidelines and may request the inclusion of particular clauses in the envisaged agreement. If necessary, the Commission may decide to include these in the agreement.
Authorisation of the opening of formal negotiations is subject to a number of conditions, including:
a description of the subject matter and scope of the agreement,
the number of EU countries involved and the number of countries involved.
the nature and duration of the negotiation.
If the Commission considers that the agreement does not meet the conditions laid down in the regulation, it may refuse to authorise its conclusion.
When notifying the Commission of their intention to enter into negotiations with an EU country, EU countries must only be required to inform it of elements which are of relevance for the assessment to be made by the Commission. If the EU country does not request the Commission to enter in to discussions with it within the time limit provided for in Article 2 of the Regulation, it must give a reasoned decision on the application of this regulation within 130 days of receiving the notification.
In the context of regional agreements as referred to in Article 1(b), any reference in this regulation to a Member State or a third party must be read as referring to the Member States or the third countries concerned, respectively.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
 
It entered into force on 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
The European Union has been governed by agreements between Member States and third countries for over 40 years.
For more information, see:
Judicial Cooperation in Civil Matters (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Jurisdiction: the jurisdiction and recognition of judgments of a court of law of a country.
* Recognition and enforcement: the right of a person to appeal against a judgment in civil or commercial proceedings.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2009 of 21 May 2009 on the concluding of agreements with a third state concerning matters of jurisdiction and of the recognition, enforcement and enforcement thereof (OJ L 127, 23.5.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) no 550/09 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS
  [Official Journal L 347 of 23.7.2009]
  The European Commission adopts Implementing Decision 2009/852/EC of 23 May 2009 establishing the framework for the conclusion, on behalf of the European Communities, of agreements on jurisdiction and enforcement in civil, commercial and administrative matters between the Community and third states.

Summary 151:
Statistics on migration and asylum
Statistics on immigration and migration
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 343/2003 on the collection and analysis of EU statistics on migration
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the exchange of statistics between EU countries on migration* and asylum* in the field of migration.
It repeals and repeals Council Regulation (EEC) no 311/76 on the compilation of statistics on foreign workers.
KEY POINTS
EU countries must supply to the European Commission (Eurostat) statistics on:
the number of residence permits issued to persons who are third-country nationals, disaggregated as follows:
permits issued during the reference period whereby the person is being granted permission to reside in the EU;
permits issued for specific categories of long-term visa or immigration status to be granted instead of a residence permit;
the numbers of such visas and grants of status.
The statistics must relate to reference periods of one calendar year and must be supplied to the Commission within 6 months of the end of the reference year. They must not include the number of persons who have in fact left the territory of the EU country, following an administrative or judicial decision or act, as referred to in point 1.
In addition, EU countries must provide Eurostat with the following statistics:
number of requests for taking back or taking charge of an asylum seeker,
the provisions on which the requests are based, and
the decisions taken in response to the requests;
total number of transfers to which the decisions referred to lead;
requests for information.
Eurostat must report to the Council on the use and probable effects of estimations or other methods of adapting statistics based on national definitions to comply with the harmonised definitions set out in the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2003.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve the quality of EU statistical data on migration. These include:
An Action Plan for the Collection and Analysis of Community Statistics in the Field of Migration, adopted in April 2003;
An Implementing Decision of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 and 20 June 2003 establishing a European Union statistical system for migration statistics.
For more information, see:
Migration statistics (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Migration: the movement of people, goods, services, capital, capital goods and capital movements within the European Union (EU).
* Asylum seeker: a person who poses a threat to public safety, public order, public security, public health or the economy of the country in which he or she lives or works.
* Asylum seeker: an individual who is seeking to enter or remain in another EU country under the protection of a third country.
ACT
Council Regulation (EU) No 344/2003 of 21 December 2003 laying down detailed rules on the application of Council Regulation [Official Journal L 136 of 21.12.2003].
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC] No 344 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 152:
Auditing of statutory auditors and audit firms in the European Union (EU) (Regulation (EC) No 552/2014)
Auditing and auditing of the statutory auditor and audit firm
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/34/EU on statutory audits
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the conditions for the approval of the persons responsible for carrying out the statutory audit as well as the minimum requirements for carrying it out.
It aims to ensure the independence of statutory audit** and audit* firms.
KEY POINTS
The statutory audit of cooperatives and savings banks is characterised in some EU countries by a system that does not allow them to choose their statutory auditor or audit firm freely.
The regulation establishes a procedure for the selection of a new statutory auditor. The selection of the auditor and the audit firm must be approved by the competent authorities of the EU country in which the audited entity is located. The competent authorities must cooperate with each other, where necessary, for the purpose of carrying out their supervisory duties regarding statutory audits.
In order to ensure a high level of investor and consumer confidence in the internal market by avoiding conflicts of interests, the statutory audits are subject to appropriate oversight by competent authorities which are independent from the audit profession and which have adequate capacity, expertise and resources. They must also be subject to a system of quality assurance, thus ensuring objectivity and independence.
EU countries may decide to allow statutory audits to provide certain tax and valuation services when such services are immaterial or have no direct effect, separately or in the aggregate, on audited financial statements. However, this does not constitute an infringement of any legislative or regulatory provision in force in the EU countries concerned.
A statutory audit must be carried out by a statutory auditor* or an audit firm* subject to stringent requirements. The statutory audit report must contain sufficient information on the independence and independence of the audit auditor or the auditor firm and on whether the audit was considered capable of detecting irregularities, including fraud.
An audit committee is established to ensure that the audit is carried out in accordance with the quality standards laid down in the regulation. The committee must ensure that:
the statutory auditor is independent of any conflicts of interest;
the audit report is prepared by an independent audit firm;
there is a maximum duration of a statutory audit engagement of at least 3 years for a particular auditor or a particular audit firm in the case of a cooperative or savings bank;
it is important that the role of an audit committee in the selection process is reinforced, in the interest of a more informed decision of the general meeting of shareholders or members of an audited company.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGULATION APPLY?
The legislation has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
   
 
For more information, see:
Statutory audits (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Statutory audit: an audit of a company’s financial statements, including its audited accounts.
* Audit firm: an independent firm that carries out an audit on behalf of the company or on its behalf.

Summary 153:
Conservation of marine biological resources and management of fisheries targeting them (2010-2015 CFP) (European Commission)
Conservation and management thereof (2010 - 2015 CFP).
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2010 on the conservation of marine aquatic resources
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a framework for the sustainable exploitation of stocks and marine ecosystems in European Union (EU) waters.
KEY POINTS
The scope of the CFP includes:
the conservation of living aquatic resources and the management of the fisheries targeting these;
the protection of marine ecosystems and the sustainable management of fishing activities.
The regulation applies to all fishing vessels flying the flag of the EU Member States. It does not apply to fishing vessels registered in non-EU countries.
Member States are responsible for the conservation and management measures they adopt for stocks in EU waters applicable solely to vessels flying their flag.
Fisheries must comply with the following:
a minimum conservation reference size (MCR) for each species of fish;
fishing quotas must be set according to the best available scientific and technical knowledge;
a maximum yield of fish for human consumption must not exceed the MCR;
there must be no discards of fish under the minimum MCR.
In addition, Member States must ensure that:
fisheries are managed in line with the EU’s policy on fisheries science;
they are based on the most up-to-date scientific and technological knowledge available to them;
their management programmes are coordinated with other Member States and the European Commission;
these programmes are implemented in close cooperation with the European Fisheries Agency (EFSA);
the European Commission is involved in the implementation of these programmes.
Aquaculture
The Commission is responsible for:
monitoring aquaculture production and marketing;
developing and implementing the European Aquaculture Strategy;
ensuring that the EU aquacultural sector has a level-playing field for operators and third-country operators;
promoting a level playing field for EU operators.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMISSION APPLY?
The CFP has applied since 25 March 2010 and had to become law in the Member States by 25 March 2015.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission adopted the regulation on behalf of the European Union in 2010.
For more information, see:
‘The European Fisheries Strategy’ on the Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (Euratom) No 529/2010 of 25 and 26 March 2010 on the Conservation of Marine Biological Resources and the Management of Fisheries Targeting them (OJ L 183, 26.3.2010, pp. 1-8)

Summary 154:
Common organisation of the markets in fishery and aquaculture products (CMO) (2014) (summary)
Common Organisation of the Markets in Fishery and Aquaculture Products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 establishing a common organisation of markets in fisheries and aquaquulture products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the CMO, which aims to:
ensure fair competition in the production and marketing of fishery products;
improve the conditions for the placing on the market of their members’ products; and
promote the sustainability of these products.
KEY POINTS
The CMO is an integral part of the Common Fisheries Policy (CFP) and should contribute to achieving the objectives of the CFP.
It is composed of:
fishery producers organisations (FPOs);
aquaculture producer organisations (PAOs); and
marketing standards.
Fishery producer organisations and PAOs are recognised in one or more EU countries and recognised in accordance with Section II of the regulation.
Member organisations must, in addition to the objectives laid down in paragraphs 1 and 2, pursue two or more of the following objectives:
improving the market conditions for their members' fishery or aquacultural products, in particular by:
providing clear information on the ecological sustainability of such products,
promoting the economic returns of producers;
contributing to food supply and promoting high food quality and safety standards, whilst contributing to environmental protection measures;
supporting the development of sustainable products, including:
research and development programmes;
promotional activities;
exchange of information and best practices;
the exchange of information;
market intelligence.
PAOs may also pursue other complementary activities, including the following:
promotion of sustainable fishing gear;
encouraging the use of selective fishing gear that will prevent under-sized fish from being caught;
ensuring the sustainable management of fishing resources;
developing and promoting a sustainable approach to the management of marine resources.
Producer organisations must also:
encourage the participation of small-scale producers in the organisation of PAOs;
take account of the specific situation of producers in rural areas;
participate in the selection and organisation of producers’ organisations.
The rules on competition relating to agreements, decisions and practices referred to in Article 101 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) apply to the production or marketing of EU products. When trading in EU products with non-EU countries, the conditions must be ensured that the products comply with the same social and environmental standards as those applicable to EU products, and that these standards are respected.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULARATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission adopted the regulation on behalf of the EU.
For more information, see:
‘The Common Market in Fisheries’ on the European Commission’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 155:
Securities settlement systems — Regulation (EU) No 652/2014
Securities Settlement Systems — Regulations (EU, Euratom) No 596/2014 and (EU), Euratom
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 608/2014 on securities settlement systems
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the establishment of a European Securities Settlement System (CSD)*.
It aims to ensure that the securities settlement system (SSS) operated by the European Securities and Markets Authority (ESMA) and the European Banking Authority (EBA) are compatible with the prudential requirements of the European Financial Stability Board (ESCB).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all financial instruments that are traded on the EU’s securities settlement markets. It does not apply to transactions that are negotiated privately by the relevant parties, but executed on the trading venues regulated by Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulation No 600/2014 or to transactions executed bilaterally, but reported to a trading venue.
It applies to:
transferable securities, money-market instruments, units in collective investment undertakings and emission allowances;
transactions that are executed by a CSD in another EU country;
trading venues that are not regulated by the ESCB.
The rules apply to all securities settlement procedures, including the following:
the execution of a buy-in procedure;
the settlement instructions on the same financial instruments;
settlement of the obligation on the intended settlement date.
the acceptance of a settlement order;
by the competent authority of the host EU country of the CSD.
Settlement procedures and penalties
The procedures for settlement fails must be commensurate with the scale and seriousness of such fails whilst being scaled in such a way that maintains and protects the liquidity of the relevant financial instruments.
In order to ensure the safety of settlement, any participant in a securities settlement* system buying or selling certain financial instruments, namely transferable securities*, money market instruments, unit in collective Investment undertakings, emission allowances, should be able to settle its obligation on its intended settlement day.
EU countries must ensure that their competent authorities have access to all information concerning the activities of the competent authorities of the central securities settlement authorities of their home country.
Where a CSDs provides its services in another country, the competent national authority of that country must request from the competent competent authority in the host country all information about the activities and activities of that CSD that is of relevance to the requesting authority. This information must be provided in the form of a standardised recording, which must be made available to the authorities of that host country. It must also be provided to the European Central Bank (ECB).
The ESCB, any other bodies performing similar functions in certain EU countries or other public bodies charged with or intervening in the management of the public debt in the EU may themselves provide a number of services, such as operating a securities-settlement system, which would qualify them as CSDs. This regulation does not prevent it from accessing the information relevant for the performance of its duties, including oversight of CSDs and other financial market infrastructures.
Exemptions
The Regulation does not cover:
services provided by CSDs outside the territory of the EU, including through setting up a branch in a non-EU country; or
the services provided by non-CSDs that are provided outside the EU.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
  Ебаларскабрака барка 
For more information, see:
‘Settlement systems’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Securities settlement system: a system in which securities are settled. It is a centralised system that is used to settle all financial transactions between the parties involved in the securities market.
MAIN DOCUMENT
 Еъралка/2014/EU of the Council and of the Representatives of the Governments of the Member States meeting within the Council of 21 December 2014 on the establishment, on behalf of the Union, of a system for the settlement of securities and amending Council Regulation (EEC) no 608/2013 (OJ L 183, 1.1.2014, pp. 1-2)

Summary 156:
Cohesion Fund: transport infrastructure
Transport infrastructure
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1316/2013 establishing the Cohesion Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the European Regional Development Fund (ERDF).
It aims to provide financial support to projects in the fields of environment and trans-European networks in the area of transport infrastructure.
It repeals Regulation (EC) No 1084/2006 and repeals Decision 661/EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The EU’s cohesion fund supports transport infrastructure projects of European added value (EADV) of €10.5 billion. It is the main source of funding for the Connecting Europe Facility (CEF), which is the EU's main investment vehicle.
The EADV is designed to contribute to the sustainable development of the European transport network and to the development of Europe's economic and social cohesion. It has a budget of €8.8 billion for the period 2014-2020. The EAF supports the following types of projects:
trans-European transport infrastructure:
investment in the environment, including areas related to sustainable development and energy which present environmental benefits;
TEN-T, in compliance with the guidelines adopted by the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2013 on EU guidelines for the implementation of the EAF;
technical assistance.
Specific provisions concerning the type of activities which can be supported by the Fund are set out in Regulation (EU-specific actions as ‘investment priorities’. These include:
environmental and noise-reduction measures;
enhancing institutional capacity of public authorities and stakeholders and efficient public administration through actions to strengthen the institutional capacity and the efficiency of public administrations and public services related to the implementing of the Fund;
transport infrastructure projects which are listed in the national plan referred to in Directive 2003/87/EC (see summary);
transit infrastructure projects that are part of the framework for the European Investment Bank (EIB) and which have been approved by the Commission.
Cohesion fund support
The Cohesion fund provides financial support for the following type of projects.
Transportation infrastructure projects under the CEF:
projects in the field of environment;
projects under the framework of TEN-t, in accordance with the European Commission guidelines adopted in December 2013;
traffic management projects, which are covered by the EIB.
In addition, the EDF provides financial assistance to the European Transport Fund for the transport sector under the EAB.
Projects which fall within the scope of the EU EAF are eligible for EAF if they meet the following criteria:
they are in line with the EU strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth;
they have a positive impact on the environment and on the economy of the Member States;
the transport sector is a key element of the overall strategy for the EU, which is based on sustainable development, energy efficiency and environmental benefits.
Infrastructure projects are eligible if they have a significant impact on:
the creation of a network of roads, bridges, tunnels, underpasses, railways, airports, ports, railways and other modes of transport; and
the improvement of the efficiency and effectiveness of public transport systems.
A common set of output indicators to assess the aggregated progress at EU level of implementing operational programmes should be set up in an annex to this regulation. For common and programme-specific output indicators, baselines shall be set at zero.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The regulation entered into force on 31 December 2013.
BACKGROUND
The European Regional development fund was established by Regulation (Euratom) No 1303/2013.
For more information, see:
European Social Fund (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (U.S. 2017/1316/EU of 31 October 2017 establishing the European Social Fund and repealing Decision 2006/94/EC of 11 July 2006 establishing the Fund for Community Development (OJ L 210, 31.10.2017, pp. 1-12)

Summary 157:
The European Regional Development Fund (ERDF) — specific thematic objectives and investment priorities (2014-2020)
The European Region Development Fund: specific thematics and investments
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 laying down the specific objectives and specific investment priorities for the implementation of the European Regional development Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the specific objective of the ERDF and the investment priorities it supports.
It aims to contribute to reducing disparities between the levels of development of the various regions and to reducing the backwardness of the least favoured regions, among which particular attention is to be paid to regions which suffer from severe and permanent natural or demographic handicaps such as the northernmost regions with very low population density and island, cross-border and mountain regions.
KEY POINTS
Objectives
The ERDF is designed to:
contribute to the shift towards a low-carbon economy;
support employment-friendly growth;
promote sustainable tourism, culture and natural heritage;
encourage the conversion of declining industrial regions into urban areas.
The objectives are set out in the regulation’s thematic sections.
Investment priorities
The specific objectives are:
to contribute to the investment for growth and jobs goal;
to support innovative actions in the area of sustainable urban development.
In order to maximise their contribution to this objective, activities supporting sustainable tourism and culture should be part of a territorial strategy for specific areas, including:
the development of urban areas in urban areas;
the conversion of existing industrial regions,
the creation of new urban areas and the development of new ones.
To contribute to this goal, the European territorial cooperation goal may also support the sharing of facilities and human resources, and all types of infrastructure across borders in all regions. The ERDF may also provide financial support for projects in the field of research and innovation.
Eligibility criteria
The regulation sets out eligibility criteria for regions:
those whose GDP per capita was less than 75 % of the average for the period 2007-2013;
those with a GDP of less than 90 % for the same period;
regional regions whose GDP was more than 70 % for this period.
Rural regions
Regional regions are eligible if they have:
a population of at least 1 000,000;
a GDP of more than 25 % for 2013;
an average population per capita greater than 50 % for 2014;
are located in an area where there is a high risk of urbanisation;
have access to, and remoteness from, large markets, faced by areas with extremely low population densities.
Special objectives
The Regulation sets out special objectives concerning the outermost regions (defined in Article 349 of the Treaty on European Union (TFEU). These include:
transformation of the north-eastern regions;
rehabilitation of the south-western regions of the Iberian Peninsula and the Canary Islands;
development of the westernmost regions of France, Germany, Italy, Spain, Portugal and the United Kingdom (1).
In addition, the regulation also sets out specific objectives concerning:
sustainable urban development;
environmental protection;
smart, sustainable and inclusive growth.
Implementing measures
The Commission adopts implementing acts in accordance with Article 290 TFEU in respect of the criteria for the selection and management of innovative actions. The Commission may adopt implementing acts which supplement this regulation with certain non-essential elements, such as:
measures to improve the efficiency of the selection criteria for innovative actions;
measures for improving the quality of the information and communication provided to the public and to the European Parliament and of the Council.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2014 and had to become law in the Member States by 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Regional development fund: a European Union fund that aims to support regional development in the European Union.
* Territorial cooperation goal: the aim of which is to strengthen regional cooperation between the countries of the EU.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еォェェェ
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom and the European Economic and Social Committee of 7 January 2013 laying down specific objectives for the operation of the Regional Development Funds (2013-2014) (OJ L 183, 1.1.2014, pp. 1-2)
